## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, damping, and driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + cubic nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic position: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (coupled nonlinear terms)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**0.5 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction ŌĆö using |v| approximation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v**2 (polynomial expansion in x and v)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x┬▓) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms (c*v) represent damping/anti-damping; sign determines energy injection vs dissipation
- Products of position powers and velocity (x┬▓┬Ęv) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type systems
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c┬Ęt) or cos(c┬Ęt) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms (x┬│) with same/opposite sign as linear term distinguish hardening vs softening spring nonlinearities
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Odd powers of velocity (v┬│) in acceleration indicate nonlinear dissipation (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between time-periodic functions and position (x┬Ęcos(c┬Ęt))

By Rule 2, no asymptotic approximations are allowed.

- **Candidate 8, 16**: Has `c5*exp(c6*t)` - can set c5=0 to eliminate, but still polynomial in v.
